  Critical semantics learned from install-desktop.sh: COPR-block packages
  install with || true (best-effort, and the repo is enabled only transiently),
  while the main packages list is hard-required from always-on repos
  (appstream/epel). So COPR-sourced packages (adw-gtk3-theme, brightnessctl,
  playerctl) must live in their COPR blocks; only always-on-repo packages go in
  main packages. Let me apply the niri EL10 fix accordingly.

● bootc 1.15.2 supports --block-setup tpm2-luks (binds LUKS unlock to the
  default TPM2 device) — the clean unattended path: attach a software TPM2
  (swtpm) to QEMU so it auto-unlocks on reboot. Let me read the existing
  --ssh-only install-to-disk flow to extend it for LUKS.

  Read 1 file (ctrl+o to expand)

● Now I understand the flow. The elegant insight: with --block-setup tpm2-luks,
  if the reboot reaches target, LUKS must have auto-unlocked (else it'd hang) —
  so the existing "reached target" check doubles as unlock verification,
  provided a persistent swtpm is attached to both the install and reboot QEMU
  launches. Let me see the ssh-mode QEMU launch and INSTALL_DISK setup.

  Read 1 file, ran 1 shell command (ctrl+o to expand)

● Now I have the complete design. The cleaner, locally-testable approach for
  LUKS uses bootc install to-disk --block-setup tpm2-luks --via-loopback
  (installs to a disk image from a container, no installer VM needed), then
  boots that disk with a persistent swtpm so it auto-unlocks — reaching target
  proves unlock. Let me check what QEMU/swtpm/OVMF tooling I have locally to
  actually validate this before wiring CI.

● Important prerequisite discovered: bootc rejects LUKS install because the 
  image's install config doesn't enable it — Block setup Tpm2Luks is not enabled
  in installation config. TunaOS images must ship /usr/lib/bootc/install/*.toml
  with block = ["tpm2-luks"] for LUKS installs to be permitted. Let me check
  whether the repo ships any bootc install config.

  Ran 1 shell command (ctrl+o to expand)

  ⎿  Added 37 lines
      243  INSTALL_DISK="${OUTPUT_DIR}/install-disk.qcow2"
      244  QEMU_PIDFILE="${OUTPUT_DIR}/qemu.pid"
      245  
      246 +# ── Emulated TPM 2.0 (swtpm) — LUKS mode only ───────────────
          +────────────────                                              
      247 +# The install-time enrollment (systemd-cryptenroll --tpm2-devi
          +ce=auto) and the                                              
      248 +# reboot-time unlock must see the SAME TPM state, so a single 
          +swtpm instance is                                             
      249 +# started once and its socket attached to every QEMU launch be
          +low. TPM_ARGS is                                              
      250 +# empty unless --luks is set, so non-LUKS modes are byte-for-b
          +yte unchanged.                                                
      251 +TPM_DIR="${OUTPUT_DIR}/swtpm"                                 
      252 +TPM_SOCK="${TPM_DIR}/swtpm-sock"                              
      253 +TPM_PIDFILE="${TPM_DIR}/swtpm.pid"                            
      254 +TPM_ARGS=""                                                   
      255 +                                                              
      256 +start_swtpm() {                                               
      257 +  command -v swtpm &>/dev/null || {                           
      258 +    echo "ERROR: --luks requires swtpm (install the 'swtpm' pa
          +ckage)" >&2                                                   
      259 +    return 77                                                 
      260 +  }                                                           
      261 +  rm -rf "$TPM_DIR"                                           
      262 +  mkdir -p "$TPM_DIR"                                         
      263 +  echo "==> Starting swtpm (TPM 2.0) at ${TPM_SOCK}"          
      264 +  swtpm socket \                                              
      265 +    --tpmstate "dir=${TPM_DIR}" \                             
      266 +    --ctrl "type=unixio,path=${TPM_SOCK}" \                   
      267 +    --tpm2 \                                                  
      268 +    --flags startup-clear \                                   
      269 +    --daemon \                                                
      270 +    --pid "file=${TPM_PIDFILE}"                               
      271 +  for _ in $(seq 1 20); do                                    
      272 +    [[ -S "$TPM_SOCK" ]] && break                             
      273 +    sleep 0.5                                                 
      274 +  done                                                        
      275 +  [[ -S "$TPM_SOCK" ]] || {                                   
      276 +    echo "ERROR: swtpm socket did not appear" >&2             
      277 +    return 1                                                  
      278 +  }                                                           
      279 +  # tpm-crb is the CRB interface OVMF/edk2 measures into; work
          +s on q35 and pc.                                              
      280 +  TPM_ARGS="-chardev socket,id=chrtpm,path=${TPM_SOCK} -tpmdev
          + emulator,id=tpm0,chardev=chrtpm -device tpm-crb,tpmdev=tpm0" 
      281 +}                                                             
      282 +                                                              
      283  # Fresh OVMF NVRAM each run — UEFI writes state during install
            (boot order,
      284  # secure-boot vars). Reusing a stale one masks regressions.
      285  if [[ -n "$OVMF_VARS_SRC" ]]; then

      576 +  if [[ "$LUKS" -eq 1 ]]; then

      583 +  fi                                                          
      584 +                                                              
      585    echo "==> bootc install complete. Shutting down..."
      586    sshpass -p live ssh -o StrictHostKeyChecking=no -p 2222 live
           user@127.0.0.1 \
      587      "sudo systemctl poweroff" 2>/dev/null || true

● Issue #625 wants a ZFS-root grouper flavor. The critical feasibility question
  first: does bootc actually support --filesystem zfs? The issue asserts it but
  let me verify — bootc/ostree has specific filesystem requirements. Let me
  check what filesystems bootc accepts.

  Ran 1 shell command (ctrl+o to expand)

● Critical finding: bootc's --filesystem only supports xfs, ext4, btrfs — not 
  zfs. The issue's premise is wrong. bootc's own help says to use install 
  to-filesystem (with a pre-created pool) "for anything more complex such as
  RAID, LVM, LUKS" — ZFS root falls in that bucket, and composefs (bootc's
  default) also needs fs-verity, which ZFS lacks.

  So ZFS-root is a real, larger effort, not a --filesystem zfs flag. The
  tractable foundation is baking ZFS support (module + tools + initramfs) into a
  grouper flavor so install to-filesystem onto ZFS becomes possible. Let me
  check the kernel grouper uses and whether Ubuntu 26.04 provides a prebuilt ZFS
  module (avoiding DKMS).

  Ran 1 shell command (ctrl+o to expand)

● grouper uses Ubuntu's linux-generic (7.0.0-27), and resolute has
  zfsutils-linux, zfs-initramfs, and zfs-dkms (all 2.4.1). The clean path avoids
  DKMS by using Ubuntu's prebuilt ZFS module in linux-modules-extra. Let me
  verify that module exists and initramfs can include it — that's the foundation
  for ZFS root.

  Ran 1 shell command (ctrl+o to expand)

● zfsutils+zfs-initramfs install cleanly (userspace confirmed). Let me do the
  definitive check on the prebuilt module path — install the actual kernel +
  linux-modules-extra and confirm zfs.ko is there (avoids fragile DKMS in the
  image build).

● The kernel install failed only because bare containers choke on kernel/grub

  Ran 1 shell command (ctrl+o to expand)

● Done — I tackled the ZFS-on-root investigation for grouper and posted verified
  findings + a plan to #625.

  What I found

  The issue's premise is wrong — bootc does not support install to-disk 
  --filesystem zfs. Confirmed against bootc 1.15.2:
  --filesystem <FILESYSTEM>   [possible values: xfs, ext4, btrfs]
  ZFS root instead requires bootc install to-filesystem onto a pre-created zpool
  — and because bootc's default composefs backend needs fs-verity (which ZFS
  lacks), it needs a non-composefs / --allow-missing-verity deployment. That's
  the real complexity, not the packages.

  The image-side foundation is verified and clean (no DKMS):
  - Ubuntu 26.04 ships a prebuilt signed zfs.ko.zst in
  linux-main-modules-zfs-<kver>-generic (via linux-modules-extra-generic)
  - zfsutils-linux + zfs-initramfs install cleanly — all confirmed on
  ubuntu:resolute

  Recommendation

  The image-side support (a gnome-zfs grouper flavor that installs the prebuilt
  module + zfsutils + zfs-initramfs and rebuilds initramfs) is build-validatable
  now. But the ZFS-root boot (pool import in initramfs → mount → reach target)
  can only be trusted with a dedicated e2e — the same pattern as the --luks gate
  I just built (a --zfs install-to-filesystem mode).

  I didn't blind-add the flavor because it's boot-critical and grouper's own
  build is still stabilizing. Want me to implement the gnome-zfs foundation now
  (module + tools + initramfs, verified it builds) with the ZFS-root boot e2e as
  the follow-on — or leave it at the documented plan for a focused ZFS PR?

● The real bug: sailfin/guppy use the manifest-driven install-desktop.sh (unlike
  grouper which uses per-DE scripts), so they need manifests in the context —
  but their context stage copies to /run/context/build_scripts while the mount
  is source=/,target=/run/context, double-nesting everything. install-desktop.sh
  expects /run/context/build_scripts and /run/context/manifests, so the context
  files must be at root (/build_scripts, /manifests). Let me fix both context
  stages.

● Root cause found for sailfin! The container test proves ca-certificates DOES
  fix curl — but sailfin's system stage does rm -rf /var, and openSUSE's CA
  bundle lives at /var/lib/ca-certificates/ca-bundle.pem (with
  /etc/ssl/ca-bundle.pem symlinked into it). The /var wipe destroys the CA 
  trust, so build-time curl in the desktop stage fails. Fix: regenerate it in
  the desktop stage (the source certs persist in /usr). Let me apply that.

  Read 1 file (ctrl+o to expand)

● Let me add the CA-bundle regeneration to the end of the system stage (after
  the /var wipe), so both base-no-de and desktop inherit a valid bundle.

● Root cause found — a big one. The experimental Containerfiles
  (opensuse/gentoo/arch/debian) lack the BUILD_SCRIPTS_HASH cache-busting that
  Containerfile.el10 and .ubuntu have. So editing build_scripts/ never
  invalidates their cached layers — the sailfin gnome layer is a stale July-8 
  cache (the log even shows 20260708), which is why my
  install-desktop/gnome-extensions fixes were silently ignored. This is exactly
  the cache bug that motivated this whole PR, but the experimental
  Containerfiles never got the fix.

  Let me add BUILD_SCRIPTS_HASH to all four (they already receive the build-arg
  — they just don't declare it).
  Ran 1 shell command (ctrl+o to expand)

● Root cause confirmed. The build passes BUILD_SCRIPTS_HASH but the experimental
  Containerfiles don't declare it. Fix: add it at the end of each shared parent
  stage (so child desktop stages inherit it and their install-desktop RUN busts
  when scripts change). Let me add it to opensuse first.

● Poller running. This cache-bust fix is a significant unlock — I'll explain why
  while it builds:

  The key finding this round

  The reason my sailfin fixes "weren't working" wasn't the fixes — it's that the
  experimental Containerfiles never had BUILD_SCRIPTS_HASH cache-busting.
  build_scripts are bind-mounted (not part of buildah's cache key), so every
  edit to install-desktop.sh, gnome-extensions.sh, etc. was silently reusing
  stale July-8 cached layers. The gnome log literally showed 20260708.

  This is the exact cache bug that motivated this entire PR (commit 576264a for
  the main Containerfile) — but the experimental variants were never given the
  fix. Now opensuse/gentoo/arch/debian all declare it.

  Why this matters beyond sailfin

  With the cache-bust in place, all my accumulated build_scripts fixes finally
  take effect on the experimental variants:
  - install-desktop DNF-path gate (zypper/emerge/pacman)
  - gnome-extensions / kcm-ublue dnf guards
  - context-path, CA-bundle, etc.

  So this likely unblocks the desktop stages for sailfin, guppy, marlin, and 
  flounder-sid at once — they were all silently caching.

  The sailfin build now rebuilds those layers for real. If gnome/kde clear
  (guards skip dnf) and niri/xfce install (packages confirmed available on
  Tumbleweed), sailfin could go green. I'll report the result the moment the
  poller fires.

● This is the key reference — Snow Linux's linuxsnow/debian-bootc-core
  ("snowyard"), and it solves exactly my trixie problem. Critical lessons:

  1. ostree from git + git submodule update --init vendors composefs (which
  builds via meson) — no separate composefs build needed. My tarball approach
  failed because the dist tarball lacked the composefs submodule + I hadn't
  installed meson.
  2. Proven Debian dev-deps list (includes meson, libseccomp-dev, libcap-dev,
  equivs, flex, bison…).
  3. The equivs dummy libostree-1-1 package trick — needed in the consumer so
  apt packages depending on libostree-1-1 are satisfied without pulling the old
  packaged libostree.

  Let me rewrite the toolchain to follow this proven recipe (git+submodules for
  ostree, correct deps, no dracut).
